French Air Minister Visits Rome; Has an Important Mission; Seeks Cooperation in French and Italian Civil Aviation; And Discusses Sky Pact Issues 39

French Villacoublay: Air Minister General Denain departed from the airfield here this morning for Rome, scheduled to arrive at the Marignane airfield near Marseilles at 11:00 am. The aircraft was piloted by Rossi, who set a long-distance flight record. In addition, the chief secretary of the Ministry of Aviation, de Stan, and the director of the Civil Aviation Bureau, Guimier, went to Italy in two other aircraft. One of the aircraft was piloted by the famous aviator Mermoz. (Havas dispatch from the 9th)

(Paris) The Air Minister's mission includes three items: (1) To seek close cooperation in French and Italian civil aviation undertakings and to negotiate an agreement on air routes between Paris, Rome, and South America. According to the plan, General Berlocchini, the Director of the Italian Civil Aviation Bureau, recently came to Paris and agreed with the French government on the basis of cooperation between the two countries on this air route. The air route from Paris to Rome may be officially opened on June 1. The route is jointly operated by France and Italy, with two round trips each week. The flight from Paris to Rome takes eight hours, with stops in Lyon and Marseilles, and flies over the French-Italian border Riviera area to avoid flying over the sea. However, the time at which the line flies over the restricted flight zone of fortresses in both countries should be agreed upon by the aviation authorities of the two countries. (2) The Sky Mutual Assistance Pact issue. According to the decision of the Stresa Conference, if Germany fails to participate in the Sky Mutual Assistance Pact recommended in the London Declaration, then the UK, France, Italy, Belgium, and other countries can conclude bilateral treaties to stipulate air force mutual assistance methods. This also requires detailed consultations between the French Air Minister and the Italian government. (3) France and Italy discussed issues related to the aviation technology cooperation between the two countries last year. These issues must continue to be discussed. In addition, Denain and French aviation personnel will also visit Italian aircraft manufacturing plants and factories. (Havas dispatch from the 8th)

British Actively Expanding Air Force, Aiming for Parity with French Strength 40

(London) February 3rd. The Anglo-French London Declaration, involving the Sky Pact, general disarmament convention, Germany's return to the League of Nations, and the conclusion of the Central European Pact, etc. It is heard that before the British government discusses other issues with France and Italy, it should consult with those countries on the air force issue. The Daily Telegraph reports that when discussing the Sky Pact in the future, the British representative will propose the amount of the country's air force strength for discussion. The minimum that the UK can accept is 1,600 front-line aircraft, which is equivalent to the strength of France. Recently, the British government has been actively expanding its air force, and the progress made is quite satisfactory. Long-range, high-speed bombers have already been built. The Ministry of Aviation has also selected areas for the construction of new airfields. The recruitment of civilians has also taken various measures to accelerate the realization of the air force plan. It is expected that within two years, the strength of the British air force will reach its maximum. (Havas dispatch, 9th)

British House of Commons Postpones Debate on National Defense 41

Baldwin and Eden to Succeed as Prime Minister and Foreign Secretary

Aviation Minister Lord Londonderry and War Secretary Lord Hailsham will both leave office and be replaced by Colonial Secretary Listowel and Dominions Secretary James. Anniversary of the British King's Coronation. Parliamentarians Present Congratulatory Addresses, Ceremony Held Yesterday at Westminster Abbey, Solemn Ceremony Filled with Praises 45

(London) Today, the King and Queen traveled by car from Buckingham Palace to Westminster Hall to receive congratulatory addresses from members of both houses of Parliament. The ceremony was extremely grand. Representatives from all parts of the Empire, 464 nobles, 455 members of the House of Commons, former cabinet members, judges, and civil officials crowded the hall. Members were seated in batches. The nobles sat on red leather chairs, and the mace of the House of Lords was placed on a large red cushion. Members of the House of Commons sat on green chairs, and the mace of the House of Commons was placed on a table. Cabinet members sat in the front two rows. Officials from the Dominions and Indian princes were seated in the visitors' gallery. All members were dressed in formal attire, resplendent in gold and jade, adding to the solemnity. The weather was gloomy that day, but when the King and Queen arrived, the clouds suddenly cleared. The road through which the royal carriage passed had been crowded with people for hours. Although there was a cool breeze, the carriage moved very slowly. The King frequently removed his crown to respond to the cheers of the people and to allow them to see his countenance. After the King and Queen entered the hall and took their seats, the Lord Chancellor Sankey first read the congratulatory address from the House of Lords. After reading, he prayed for blessings for the King. Next, the Speaker of the House of Commons, FitzRoy, read the congratulatory address from the House of Commons. Both addresses were filled with praise. Finally, the King delivered a speech expressing his thanks. The address from the House of Lords took seven minutes to read, and the address from the House of Commons took five minutes to read. The King's speech lasted exactly ten minutes. First, he thanked the officials for gathering here today to offer congratulations, and he especially welcomed the representatives from India. He then said that in recent years, political upheavals had destroyed other empires and freedoms, but the complete harmony of the British parliamentary system and its constitutional monarch remained firmly in place, which was something to be proud of and thankful for. The ancient British constitution was always adapted to various changes. During his 25 years on the throne, he had encountered and overcome wars that previous generations could not have imagined, and he had faced new demands for democracy at home and abroad. He then spoke of the prosperous era of Queen Victoria, and then spoke of how external threats often united all parties, classes, governments, and ethnic groups in the Empire, and how men and women all did their duty, which he would never forget. He then expressed sympathy for the unemployed and finally thanked the Queen for her help. After the ceremony, the band played "God Save the King." After the music ended, the Lord Chancellor asked the crowd to shout "Long live the King" three times, which they did in unison. This was an unprecedented event. The ceremony lasted a total of 30 minutes. Then, the bells of Westminster Abbey rang out, and the King and Queen returned to the palace by carriage. Cheers erupted outside the hall. London will still be brightly lit tonight. (Reuters dispatch, 9th)

(London) Today is the third day of the British King's Silver Jubilee week, and the excitement of the people has not diminished. In the evening, thousands of people flocked to the West End again to see the lights, and the excitement was no less than on the night of the 6th. Although there was a cool breeze tonight, tens of thousands of people still gathered outside Buckingham Palace, cheering incessantly. The King and Queen appeared on the balcony at 9:30, waving frequently for several minutes. It is estimated that there were more than 50,000 people outside the palace, and the cheers continued for five minutes without interruption. When Prince Gloucester also appeared on the balcony, the crowd became even more excited. A thanksgiving service was held at County Hall tonight, attended by 8,000 people. Tomorrow is the 25th anniversary of the King's coronation, and both houses of Parliament will present congratulatory addresses to the King and Queen. All arrangements have been completed and the ceremony is scheduled to be held in Westminster Hall. The entire cabinet will also attend. According to Speaker of the House of Commons FitzRoy today, he will personally read the congratulatory address in his capacity as Speaker of the House of Commons. Prime Minister MacDonald today moved in the House of Commons that a congratulatory address should be presented to the King, which was unanimously passed by the entire House. At the same time, War Secretary Hailsham also made the same motion in the House of Lords, which was also unanimously passed, in order to express the sincerity of the two houses through praise. (Reuters dispatch, 8th)

Madrid. After the formation of the coalition cabinet organized by Prime Minister Lerroux, he attended the Chamber of Deputies today and delivered a policy statement of the new cabinet, which stated: "Spiritual peace, and the harmonious cooperation of Spanish people who are law-abiding, is the motto that the government adheres to. The various disputes of the past should be put behind us. The authority of the government should be strengthened, the foundation of the republic must be consolidated, and social and economic order must be restored to normal as soon as possible. All of these are the goals of the new government. The new cabinet is not a party cabinet, and its members all have strong and loyal political sentiments. The facts will demonstrate this. We are not socialists, but we believe that it is necessary to adopt measures to achieve social justice and eliminate class struggle. The government's primary concern will be to alleviate unemployment panic. When municipal elections are held in the autumn of this year, the government will submit a draft constitutional reform. (Paris) Kerensky, the first Prime Minister of Russia, who is now in exile here, declared to a United Press interviewer today that Japan has assured European countries that no war will occur between Japan and Russia, because the pledge of peace between the two countries is very firm. Reuter's Special Business Telegram, May 9th 108

Gold and Silver

London Gold Market: Today it is easing, the price is 6.57, the same as yesterday's price, at 143 shillings 8 pence, falling by 4.5 pence.

London Silver Market: Silver prices fell 3125 today, the spot price is 3 - 2.5 pence, and the futures price is 32.6875 pence. The drop in silver prices is due to selling by China, India, and speculators, but China, India, and speculators later repurchased. The market closed steady.

Mount Isa Silver: Continued to fall today, the opening price shrunk by 15 pounds and became 72.75.

Exchange Rates

US Dollar: In the London foreign exchange market, the British-US exchange rate opened lower than yesterday's closing rate by 125. Later, due to purchases of the British pound, sentiment stabilized and prices tended to rise. In the afternoon, the price was 4 dollars, 84.875 cents, 0.5 cents higher than the opening price, and one US dollar equaled 4 shillings, 1.497 pence.

British France: The opening price was 73 francs 46, an increase of 5 pounds. The price continued to rise in the morning, and at 2 pm, the price was 73 francs 57, an increase of 11 pounds compared to the opening price.

Cotton and Wheat

New York Cotton Market: The opening was stable. Because the theory of inflation may be revived, the news that the US cotton public storage agency sold spot cotton caused the bulls to close out. Due to the emergence of speculative buying, cotton prices became firm. Very little was sold in the near term, and demand was silent in the long term due to better weather reports.

Chicago Wheat: Steady today, opening prices are the same as yesterday. There was not much fluctuation in the morning, and interest from peers was not strong. It is believed that the wheat market sold through winter, and the weather conditions are said to be still good. The miscellaneous grains market is very sluggish.

Liverpool Cotton: Continued to be sluggish today, the July term at 1 pm.

New York: The market is stable today and trading is sluggish. Prices did not improve much in the morning.

The Rotation Period for the Security Forces in the War Zone Has Been Determined 109

The Security Forces Will Be Renamed as Special Police Force, and the Provincial Government Has Ordered That the Rotation Will Be on the 11th

Beiping Communication: The Chinese and Japanese representatives held talks in Tianjin on the 6th and 7th regarding the rotation of the security forces in the war zone. The results were satisfactory. Gao Jitan, the military attaché of the Japanese embassy, and Yin Rugeng, the commissioner of the Ji-Mi District, returned to Beiping last night (7th) and this morning (8th), respectively. After getting off the train, Yin went to the Political Readjustment Council to visit Chief Advisor Wang Kemin to report on the talks with the Japanese side in Tianjin. It is reported that during the Tianjin talks, after the Japanese representative Yoshii Seiya met with Yu Xuezhong, Chairman of the Hebei Provincial Government, all issues were resolved smoothly. The rotation of the security forces has been decided to start on the 11th of this month. The provincial government issued orders separately today (the day). The new team under Zhang Qingyu was renamed the First General Detachment of the Hebei Provincial Special Police Force, and the team under Zhang Yantian was renamed the Second General Detachment. The two teams will start from Cai Village and Cangzhou on the 11th and concentrate in Tongzhou and Tangshan. Zhang Qingyu's team is moving on foot, and Zhang Yantian's team is going by special Beining train. After concentrating in Tongzhou and Tangshan, they will set off to their designated defense areas separately. It is expected to take three weeks to complete. The old teams under Fan Jinghua and Yang Yucheng will also concentrate in Tongzhou and Tangshan after the new teams take over the defense areas, and then leave the "war zone" and return to their original organization. Secondly, it was agreed that the three teams under Zhou Yuying, Liu Zuozhou, and Zhao Lei would remain in their original defense areas for the time being and would not be transferred. The numbers of the three teams have also been decided to be renamed the Third Team, Fourth Team, and Fifth Team of the Hebei Provincial Special Police Force. With unified names, command will be more convenient. As for the headquarters of the first and second general detachments, it has been decided that the first general detachment will be located in Jixian County, and the second general detachment will be located in Liushouying. The locations of the headquarters of the third, fourth, and fifth general detachments will be determined after the defense areas are newly demarcated. Yin Rugeng paid a visit to He Yingqin again this afternoon (8th) to ask for instructions and is scheduled to go to Tongzhou tomorrow (9th) to preside over the matter. Regarding the reduction of the Li Yunsheng team (formerly stationed in Yutian) currently stationed in Xiasi and Yanjiao, the procedures have been completed today (8th). It was originally scheduled to implement the reorganization on the 11th, but since the rotation period is also on the 11th, the authorities will advance the procedure for safety reasons. If it is not possible, it will be slightly delayed. Once the rotation of the security forces is completed, the cleaning work in the "war zone" will only have the task of taking over the Eastern Tombs left. (8th)

The Legislative Yuan Passes the Central Bank Law 110

The Legislative Yuan, in its sixteenth meeting on the ninth of this month, passed the Central Bank Law. The full text comprises thirty-six articles, which are recorded as follows: Chapter I, General Provisions, Article 1: The Central Bank is a national bank established by the National Government. Article 2: The National Government grants the Central Bank the following exclusive rights: 1. Issuing convertible banknotes for standard currency and subsidiary currency. 2. Managing the issuance of standard currency and subsidiary currency coined by the government, and managing the minting of standard currency upon public request. 3. Managing the national treasury. 4. Underwriting domestic and foreign debts and handling matters related to repayment of principal and payment of interest. Article 3: The Central Bank shall establish its head office in the capital and branches in various locations within the country, and may establish agencies in necessary locations abroad. Article 4: The establishment or abolition of Central Bank branches and overseas agencies must be decided by the board of directors and reported to the National Government for record. Article 5: The Central Bank shall have a business term of thirty years from the date of implementation of this law. Two years before the expiration of the term, it may apply to the National Government for approval to extend it.

Chapter II, Capital. Article 6: The total capital of the Central Bank shall be 100 million silver dollars, to be fully allocated by the national treasury. Article 7: When necessary, the Central Bank may, upon resolution of the board of directors and consent of the board of supervisors, apply to the National Government for approval to expand the total capital and may solicit commercial shares. However, the total number of commercial shares shall not exceed 40% of the total capital. When soliciting commercial shares, legal entities operating in the banking and financial industry in this country should be given priority to subscribe. Only after the commercial shares purchased by various legal entities have reached 30% or more of the total capital of the Central Bank, can domestic or individual citizens invest. However, individual citizen investment shall be subject to the approval of the Minister of Finance. Chapter III, Organization. Article 8: The Central Bank shall establish a board of directors, composed of eleven to fifteen directors specially appointed by the National Government. Among them, there should be individuals actually engaged in agriculture, industry, commerce, and banking, with each having at least one representative. The term of office for each director shall be three years, and they may be reappointed upon expiration of the term. The board of directors shall have five to seven standing directors, designated by the National Government from among the directors. The number of directors and the method of selection mentioned above shall be separately determined when soliciting commercial investment. Article 9: The Central Bank shall have one president, specially appointed, and two vice presidents, simply appointed. The term of office for each shall be three years, and they may be reappointed upon expiration of the term. Article 10: The Central Bank shall establish a board of supervisors, composed of seven supervisors specially appointed by the National Government. Among them, there should be one individual each actually engaged in agriculture, industry, commerce, and banking, and one representative dispatched by the auditing agency of the National Government. The term of office for supervisors, except for the one dispatched by the auditing agency, shall be one year for the remaining two. However, there shall be three supervisors with a one-year term in each term of supervisors, designated by the National Government. The chairman of the board of supervisors shall be elected by the supervisors from among themselves. The provisions of Article 8, paragraph 2, shall apply mutatis mutandis to this article. Article 11: The president shall manage all affairs of the bank, and the vice presidents shall assist the president in handling all affairs of the Bank. The president shall be the chairman of the board of directors. In the absence of the president, the vice president shall act as chairman. Article 12: The following matters shall be executed by the president after being resolved by the board of directors: 1. Business policy. 2. Amount of banknotes to be issued. 3. Amount of reserves. 4. Budget and final accounts. 5. Expansion of capital. 6. Enactment of various regulations. 7. Establishment and abolition of domestic branches and overseas agencies. 8. Matters proposed by the president. Article 13: The duties of the board of supervisors are as follows: 1. Auditing of accounts. 2. Inspection of reserves. 3. Inspection of the amount of banknotes issued. 4. Review of the budget and final accounts. Article 14: The head office affairs of the Central Bank may, with the approval of the National Government, establish bureaus and offices to handle them. The directors, deputy directors, chiefs, and deputy chiefs of the aforementioned bureaus and offices shall be appointed by the president with the consent of the board of directors. Article 15: Each bureau and office of the Central Bank's head office may handle affairs by division. The directors and deputy directors of each division shall be appointed by the president. Article 16: The managers of the Central Bank's branches shall be appointed by the president with the consent of the board of directors.

Chapter IV, Exclusive Rights. Article 17: The maximum amount of banknotes issued by the Central Bank shall be subject to the approval of the National Government. Article 18: The Central Bank may issue banknotes for standard currency in denominations of one yuan, five yuan, ten yuan, fifty yuan, and one hundred yuan. The Central Bank may issue banknotes for decimal subsidiary currency. Article 19: Central Bank banknotes are legal tender, uniformly circulating throughout the country regardless of region. Article 20: Central Bank banknotes shall be redeemed by the head office with silver standard currency. Article 21: Central Bank banknotes shall be exempt from banknote issuance tax. Article 22: The reserve fund for Central Bank banknotes shall have at least 60% cash reserve. The remainder shall be guaranteed by securities issued or guaranteed by the National Government, and negotiable instruments that meet the requirements of Article 27, items 5 and 7, shall be used as guaranteed reserves. Article 23: Cash reserves are divided into the following two types: 1. Silver standard currency and mint bars held in the bank's vault. 2. Raw gold and silver held in the bank's vault or deposited in other reputable banks. The raw gold and silver mentioned in item 12 above shall be converted at market prices. Article 24: The reserve fund for Central Bank banknotes shall be fully disclosed. The amount of banknotes issued and the amount of reserves shall be published weekly. Article 25: The issuance of standard and subsidiary currency or mint bars by the National Government, and the minting of standard currency or mint bars upon public request, shall be managed by the Central Bank. Article 26: All receipts and payments of funds for the national treasury and state-owned enterprises shall be managed by the Central Bank. The receipts and payments of funds for provincial, municipal, and county treasuries and their public enterprises may be handled by the Central Bank as an agent. In places where the Central Bank has not established branches, the affairs in the first item may be handled by other banks entrusted by the Central Bank. Article 27: When the National Government raises domestic and foreign debt, it shall be entrusted to the Central Bank for underwriting. All matters related to repayment of principal and payment of interest shall be managed by the Central Bank. However, when necessary, the Central Bank may entrust other banks to jointly underwrite or manage them.

Chapter V, Business. Article 28: The business of the Central Bank is as follows: 1. Receiving and storing deposits. 2. Custody of legal reserve funds of various banks. 3. Handling clearing of negotiable instruments and interbank transfers and settlements. 4. Rediscounting of treasury bills and public bond interest coupons issued or guaranteed by the National Government. The maturity date of the securities and interest coupons mentioned above shall not exceed six months from the date of rediscount. 5. Rediscounting of domestic bank acceptance bills, domestic commercial drafts, and promissory notes. The negotiable instruments mentioned above must be for the production, manufacture, transportation, or sale of goods, and their maturity date shall not exceed six months from the date of acquisition by the Bank, and shall have the signatures of at least two reputable commercial firms. However, if bills of lading, warehouse receipts, or storage receipts are attached as collateral, and the value of the goods exceeds 25% of the amount of the negotiable instrument, the signature of one reputable commercial firm is also acceptable. 6. Trading drafts for foreign payments. The foreign drafts mentioned above, if arising from import and export trade, shall not have a maturity date exceeding four months after sight. If they are acceptance bills, their maturity date shall not exceed four months from the date of acquisition by the Bank. All drafts with payment dates determined according to commercial practice shall have the signatures of at least two reputable commercial firms. However, if bills of lading, warehouse receipts, or storage receipts are attached as collateral, and the value of the goods exceeds 25% of the amount of the negotiable instrument, the signature of one reputable commercial firm is also acceptable. 7. Buying and selling sight drafts and checks of reputable domestic and foreign banks. 8. Buying and selling public bonds and treasury bills issued or guaranteed by the National Government. The amount shall be determined by the board of directors. 9. Buying and selling raw gold and silver and foreign currencies. 10. Handling domestic and foreign remittances and issuing bank drafts. 11. Making loans secured by raw gold and silver. 12. Making loans secured by public bonds and treasury bills issued or guaranteed by the National Government. The amount, term, and interest rate shall be determined by the board of directors. 13. Trust business entrusted by the government. Article 29: The Central Bank's rediscount rate shall be announced by the president after being resolved by the board of directors or the standing board of directors. The rediscount rate of the branches shall be determined by the head office's standard, and the local branches shall determine and announce it according to the local financial situation. Article 30: The Central Bank's acquisition of real estate shall be limited to the following items: 1. Real estate necessary for the Bank's business operations. 2. Real estate acquired due to debt repayment. The real estate mentioned in item 2 above shall be disposed of within one year from the date of acquisition. However, in special circumstances, it may be extended upon resolution of the board of directors. Article 31: The Central Bank's business shall be subject to the following restrictions: (1) The loan term shall not exceed six months. (2) The total amount of loans, rediscounts, or other advances and purchases of drafts, checks, or other negotiable instruments for private individuals or companies and other private legal entities shall not exceed 500,000 yuan per household. If it is a limited company, it shall not exceed one-third of the company's total capital and reserve fund. (3) The following types of negotiable instruments shall not be purchased or rediscounted, or used as ancillary collateral for other loans, except for additional collateral or for the purpose of protecting the Bank's interests, in which case it is not limited. They shall be disposed of within one year from the date of acquiring such negotiable instruments: A. Negotiable instruments arising from long-term investments for the purpose of purchasing real estate, mineral properties, housing, machinery, etc. B. Negotiable instruments arising for consumption purposes and not used for current business needs. C. Negotiable instruments arising for speculative trading. (4) Goods shall not be accepted as collateral for loans. (5) It shall not directly engage in various industrial and commercial enterprises. (6) It shall not provide guarantees for third parties or accept negotiable instruments. (7) It shall not provide credit loans or overdrafts. (8) It shall not engage in businesses of a speculative nature.

Chapter VI, Final Accounts and Reports. Article 32: The Central Bank shall have an annual final account period at the end of December each year. It shall prepare the following list of books and documents, submit them to the board of directors for resolution and the board of supervisors for review, and report them to the National Government for record: (1) Inventory of assets. (2) Balance sheet of assets and liabilities. (3) Business report. (4) Profit and loss statement. (5) Surplus distribution statement. The balance sheet of assets and liabilities and the profit and loss statement mentioned above shall be published in the National Government Gazette and newspapers in the location of the head office and branches. Article 33: For each final account, the Central Bank shall set aside 50% or more of the net profit as a public reserve fund. When the public reserve fund reaches the total capital, the fixed rate may be reduced to 25% or more upon resolution of the board of directors and consent of the board of supervisors. Article 34: In addition to setting aside a public reserve fund from the Central Bank's net profit, the president may propose to the board of directors to set aside a certain amount from the remaining balance for employee welfare funds. The remaining balance shall be turned over to the national treasury. The employee welfare funds mentioned above shall not exceed one-quarter of the total annual salaries. Article 35: After the Central Bank solicits commercial shares in accordance with the provisions of Article 7, the dividend shall be determined separately. However, the provisions of the preceding two articles regarding the setting aside of public reserve funds and employee welfare funds shall not be changed.

Chapter VII, Supplementary Provisions. Article 36: This law shall be implemented from the date of promulgation.

County Magistrates from Five Provinces to be Transferred to Lushan for Strict Training; Training Period to be Two Months 111

Nanchang dispatch: Chairman Chiang has been advocating for reform of the political system, especially in county administration. He has paid special attention to improving the status of county magistrates, strictly defining the selection of county magistrates, and increasing funding for county governments, among other improvements. Given the inconsistent levels of county magistrates in the bandit suppression provinces, it has been decided that during the summer of this year, county magistrates from Henan, Hubei, Anhui, Jiangxi, and Fujian provinces will be transferred to Lushan in batches for strict training for a period of two months. The subjects will include spiritual lectures, county administration research, etc. Chiang has also instructed Gan Naiguang, director of the Sixth Department of the General Headquarters, and Xiong Shihui to formulate specific measures and submit them for approval, so as to issue a circular to various provinces for compliance.

Further dispatch: Jiangxi Province was originally a military area for bandit suppression. After seven or eight years of devastation by bandits, the counties are in dire straits. Capable and strong county magistrates are needed to clear out bandits, reorganize, provide post-disaster relief, stabilize the area, and seek recovery to achieve revival. Therefore, Provincial Chairman Xiong Shihui previously established a County Administration Research Class and a County Administration Personnel Training Institute to cultivate lower-level political cadres. Three sessions have already been completed. Now, following Chairman Chiang's order, all eighty-three county magistrates in the province will be transferred to the provincial capital in batches for training. Section chiefs and secretaries of county governments are also included in the training. The first batch of county magistrates to be transferred to the provincial capital includes those from Linchuan, Yushan, and Duchang counties, and classes will begin on May 1st. The training period will be two months. After the first batch graduates, the second and third batches will be held, until all county magistrates have completed the training. It is heard that in the future, the county magistrates will also be transferred to Lushan in batches for special training by the General Headquarters to create strong political cadres. In addition, Jiangxi Province will follow Chiang's order to abolish bureaus and establish sections in each county, and set up district offices. This will be implemented starting from the 25th year and completed in three phases starting from July 1st (May 7th).

Jiading: Provincial Civil Affairs Department Inspector Visits the County 112

Zhang Qingyuan, an inspector from the Provincial Department of Civil Affairs, arrived in Jiading on the evening of the 7th and stayed at the Nanyang Hotel. On the morning of the 8th, he went to the county government and then inspected the Public Security Bureau, the prison, the farmers' bank, etc. On the 9th, together with Zhou Huawen, a provincial Baojia guidance officer, he inspected the county education bureau, etc. He greatly praised the county's central district education system. It is heard that he will also go to various districts to conduct a detailed inspection of the autonomous education situation. He is scheduled to stay in Jiading for ten days.

Three Baojia Census Officers Dismissed and Transferred 113

The Baojia census in this county is being supervised and guided by Provincial Guidance Officer Zhou Huawen and County Magistrate Xu Cixuan. It has already progressed to the third stage of signing contracts for joint security. Starting from the 6th of this month, it is the period for the county government and the provincial guidance officer to review the results. However, the review revealed that the second, third, and fourth districts in the county all had discrepancies. Magistrate Xu was very displeased and ordered that Feng Jiarui, the census officer of the second district, be dismissed and replaced by Wei Zecha. District Chief Gu Yaoxing received a demerit. Wu Fuzeng, the census officer of the third district, was dismissed and replaced by Yin Xinyuan. District Chief Xu Yuanchou was replaced. Zhu Xiejun, the census officer of the fourth district, was dismissed and replaced by Liu Yinghua. District Chief Xu Jiaqiu received a reprimand.

Wuxi: The Poison Pill King Was Arrested Yesterday and Taken to Wuxi 114

Wang Guiqing, the main culprit in the case of manufacturing "Renma Pi" (meaning "people and horse spleen") poison pills in this county, was arrested by detectives from the Public Security Bureau on the 6th at No. 36 Hongxiang Lane, Changsha Road, Xinzha Road, in the British Concession of Shanghai. He was escorted to the First Special Court for interrogation. The trial was conducted by Judge Yang Zhaosuo of the Eighth Criminal Court. The suspect denied being Wang Guiqing and claimed to be Zhang Kexiang. Subsequently, officials from the Public Security Bureau of this county identified him and produced a wanted photo to verify his identity. Only then did the suspect admit that his real name was Wang Guiqing and that Zhang Kexiang was his alias. The head of the detective team, Zhong J鹤, submitted an official letter for retrieval. After the judge reviewed it, he ordered that the suspect be handed over to Team Leader Xue to be taken away. Team Leader Xue handcuffed the suspect and escorted him to Wuxi by car. The suspect remained calm in the car, talking and laughing as usual. He also said that he hoped to eliminate poison pills within three years, and that his sacrifice would be insignificant. He wished to be executed in Wuxi so that he could persuade those who made "red pills," etc. After the suspect was escorted to Wuxi, Section Chief Yi interrogated him late into the night. He confessed that his accomplice was Su Guoliang (also known as Xian Lanbao), who was hiding at No. 6 Zhoushanbang. Guard Yuan Yitao and plainclothes patrolmen were dispatched to arrest him. Su was arrested at the entrance of the Wuxi Hotel and taken to the bureau for custody. It is scheduled that he will be escorted to the county government today (the 10th) for interrogation.

Changshu: Chief of Public Security Section Dismissed for Prostitution 115

Zhou Ding, the director of the Public Security Bureau, personally went to search the home of a private prostitute, Yang Fengzhu, at No. 14 Tianningsi Lane on the afternoon of the 7th. Unexpectedly, Zhou Chuanzu, the chief of the bureau's Third Section, was there. The director was extremely angry and summoned the section chief after returning to the bureau, ordering him to leave Changshu immediately and dismissing him from his post. The section chief and the director were cousins, and the section chief had been promoted from clerk to section chief. He had been greatly trusted in the past. After the section chief resigned, he handed over his duties on the morning of the 8th.

Old Guangdong Goods Store Loses Money and Closes Down 116

The Renhexiang Guangdong Goods Store, located on the west side of the Hui Ri Temple on Siqian Street, has been open in Changshu for over a century. In recent years, it has suffered huge losses due to the decline of the rural economy. The store's business strategy was also outdated and unwilling to improve, which ultimately led to its failure. It closed down on the 8th of this month and hired a lawyer to announce liquidation. All partners were also dismissed. All remaining goods will be assessed by appraisers to offset debts. It is heard that the total debt is over 20,000 yuan.

Zhenjiang: Opium Addicts' Factory to Start Construction Soon 117

The Jiangsu Provincial Anti-Opium Association has decided to convert the Baichang Yarn Factory in Xiaohai Town, Nantong District, into a vocational training factory for opium addicts. Yan Yinanu has been appointed as the director of the factory. The factory building has four large rooms, and a gym will be built for opium addicts to exercise. There will also be dormitories, offices, and bathrooms. The entire factory can accommodate 514 opium addicts. Construction will begin soon and is expected to be completed in about two months. It is said that a provincial association will also be established.

Deadline for Completion of River Dredging Project 118

The Provincial Government recently issued a circular to the counties south of the Yangtze River, stating that the province has been handling drought relief through public works, dredging the riverbanks in Zhenjiang, Jurong, Wujin, Lishui, Jintan, Yixing, Danyang, Wuxi, Liyang, and other counties south of the Yangtze River. It has been nearly five months since preparations began last winter. Repeated orders have been issued to expedite the work. Many counties have been able to enthusiastically recruit laborers and quickly respond to the situation, which is gratifying. However, as of the end of April, there were still interruptions in the labor recruitment in various counties, which prevented the completion of the project. If the obstruction in a local area leads to the failure of the entire river's access, it would be a waste of effort. Now that the busy farming season is approaching, laborers will soon be needed for farm work. If people's hearts waver, the work will inevitably slack off. It is the responsibility of the county magistrates and team leaders to supervise and urge the completion of the project within the deadline to ensure its completion. It is hereby stipulated that, except for special circumstances, all projects must be completed by May 20th. All county magistrates must immediately comply and urge the laborers to work hard to ensure completion within the deadline. The dredging of the river for public works this time is of great importance. The government will use the results of this project as an important part of the county magistrates' performance evaluation, and will reward or punish them accordingly. The government will not make any excuses and will not allow any temporary negligence to delay the overall situation.

The work of registering households for the Baojia system in this county is about to be completed in various districts. The Baojia chiefs have been elected one after another and will soon be completed. Then, he decided on 16 items for carrying out the plan. Then, Guidance Officer Xing instructed on the methods of implementation and the points to be noted in the third phase of work.

Shaoxing: County Magistrate Transferred to Implement Central County Administration 120

County Magistrate Chen Huan of Shaoxing has been ordered to transfer to Haining. The vacancy will be filled by He Yangling, the director of the Civil Affairs Department's secretariat. Magistrate Chen has now ordered various bureaus and sections to expedite the handover and is waiting for the new appointee to take over. It is heard that Magistrate He will come to Shaoxing on the 16th to take over. After taking office, he will begin to implement central county administration and make major reforms in the organizational structure. At that time, the Public Security, Finance, and Education Bureaus will be abolished and replaced with sections. All public security substations in the county will also be abolished to implement the principle of unified police and defense. Starting from the 24th year, unified accounting will be implemented. A unified expenditure system will be adopted for government expenses. All local property associations, education property associations, etc. will be abolished and merged, and a new agency will be established to manage the funds.

This year's yellow croaker season in the nine coastal areas of Nantong in northern Jiangsu Province has seen abundant production due to the pacified sea. However, fish prices are surprisingly low. According to the survey, the income from fish production has reached more than 1.3 million yuan. Currently, yellow croaker is sold on the market for three yuan per dan. Fishermen and fishmongers are all crestfallen.

Ningbo: Fire in Zhuangshi Town 126

Zhuangshi Town, under the jurisdiction of Zhenhai County, experienced a fire at the Zhu Suo Mentou area at 12:10 AM this morning (the 7th). Bamboo screens storing cold ashes in an empty house owned by the Zhuang family suddenly exploded, with dense smoke making it impossible to approach. Residents nearby were awakened from their dreams and fled with the elderly and children, their cries filling the fields. The situation was tragic. The responsible Zhuangshi Public Security Bureau and the local Yi Long rushed to gather and extinguish the fire. After two hours, the fire was finally extinguished. Eleven large buildings, including those of Zhuang Kefa, Zhuang Menghe, and Zhuang Yuefang, were burned down, totaling more than 20 rooms, with losses estimated at 40,000 to 50,000 yuan.

Haimen: Revenge Killing in Yinqiao Township 127

Cao Jinfeng, a villager of Yinqiao Township in the Fourth District, had a long-standing feud with his neighbor Zhou Weibang. On the 20th of last month, Cao's mother, Wang, had a quarrel with Zhou over a trivial matter and was beaten and injured by Zhou. She died on the 15th after medical treatment proved ineffective. Subsequently, a mediator arranged for Zhou to pay for the funeral expenses. However, the hatred between the two parties deepened. The afternoon before yesterday, Cao was returning home from shopping in Puji Town when he was stopped by Zhou in front of Zhou's house. Zhou stabbed him in the throat with a sharp blade, causing a profuse amount of blood and causing him to fall to the ground unconscious. Seeing that his goal had been achieved, Zhou fled without a trace. Cao's wife, Chen, learned of the incident and carried Cao back for treatment and reported to the county government to arrest the murderer and investigate the case.

Yesterday's "May 9th" National Humiliation Memorial: Representatives from All Sectors Held a Memorial Meeting 129

Yesterday was the "May 9th" National Humiliation Memorial Day, which is also the most painful page in our country's recent history. The Municipal Party Headquarters of this city, in accordance with the central government's regulations, held a memorial meeting yesterday morning for representatives from all sectors. The entire city lowered flags to half-mast and suspended entertainment for one day to express condolences. The Municipal Security Office, the Public Security Bureau, and the authorities of the two concessions implemented special alerts to prevent reactionary elements from causing trouble. The details are recorded separately below:

Venue Arrangement

The venue was set up in the Municipal Party Headquarters auditorium. In front of the gate hung the Party and national flags and a white cloth banner, inscribed with the words "Shanghai Representatives from All Sectors Hold National Humiliation Memorial Meeting." In the center of the auditorium hung the Party and national flags and the Premier's portrait. Order slogans were posted on both sides. Slogans were pasted all over the four walls. The scene was very solemn.

Attending Representatives

In addition to Huang Shaoxiong, representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, attendees included Qiu Yunming of the Land Bureau, Jiang Huaixu of the Defense Committee, Li Guangteng of the Municipal Education Association, Lin Kecong of the Women's Association, Lu Youchang of the Jianghai Customs Supervisory Office, Wu Zishi of the Citizens' Association for Promoting National Goods, Huang Xianggu of the Second Special District Citizens' Association, Wang Jiean of the National Goods Maintenance Association, Huang Chu of the Labor Association, Ma Hanfeng of the Labor Education Association, Zhao Erchang of the Confucius Worship and National Salvation Association, Hu Tianseng of the New Movement Association, Wu Xiu of Jinan University, Hu Xiongdong of Jiaotong University, Jiang Shouchun of Tongji University, and representatives from New Asia, Junyi, He'an, Huiqiao, and other schools, as well as various institutions, organizations, and party headquarters at all levels, totaling more than 200 people.

Meeting Order

(1) All stand at attention. (2) Sing the Party Song. (3) Pay the highest respect to the Party and national flags and the Premier's portrait. (4) Respectfully read the Premier's will. (5) Observe three minutes of silence. (6) Report. (7) Speech. (8) Shout slogans. (9) The ceremony concludes and the meeting adjourns.

Chairman's Report

After performing the ceremony, Chairman Huang Zaoxiong reported briefly: May 9th is the day when Japanese imperialists forced China to sign the Twenty-One Demands, a treaty of national subjugation. The occurrence of May 9th was by no means accidental. Since the Meiji Restoration, Japan began their so-called continental policy, following the predetermined steps, from seizing Huanqiu to signing the Twenty-One Demands, attempting to achieve the ambition of annexing China. At that time, Japan dared to boldly propose the Twenty-One Demands, firstly because the great powers were indulging in the European War, secondly because China's internal affairs were corrupt, and thirdly because Yuan Shikai hoped to realize his dream of becoming emperor. Therefore, Japan believed that this was a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity and could not sit idly by. We must wash away this great humiliation that we have suffered. I feel that to wash away this national humiliation, we must organize all the people of the country. Regardless of farmers, workers, merchants, or students, they should all have strict organizations. With everyone united and of one mind, then suppressing the bandits can certainly achieve victory, production and construction can definitely succeed, and all undertakings can be brought into line and can be expected to succeed. And all foreign aggression can also be resisted, making the Chinese nation and country stronger day by day. That's all.

Memorial Slogans

After the chairman's report, slogans were immediately shouted: (1) Swear to wash away national humiliation! (2) Strive to eliminate bandits! (3) Strive for production and construction! (4) Vigorously promote the New Life Movement! (5) Abolish unequal treaties! (6) Long live the National Revolution! (7) Long live the liberation of the Chinese nation! (8) Long live the Chinese Nationalist Party! (9) Long live the Republic of China!

National Flag Raising and Lowering Must Be Saluted: Municipal Government Ordered to Comply 130

The Shanghai Municipal Government received an instruction from the Executive Yuan, which stated: "The National Government's instruction No. 295 on April 8, 24th year of the Republic states, 'According to the report No. 1 of the Military Affairs Committee Chairman on April 4, 24th year of the Republic, 'According to the report of the Chairman of the Aviation Committee, 'According to the report of Yang Guanyu, Deputy Director of the Second Department of this Committee, 'It is found that the national flag is a symbol representing the country and embodies the national spirit. There are established ways for its use, and prescribed etiquette for welcoming and sending it off. This is to show respect and uphold the system. Currently, it is found that while most officers and soldiers in various institutions can stand at attention when the national flag is raised or lowered, the direction of the salute has not yet become uniform. This Committee is also the same. This situation indicates a lack of love, respect, and veneration. In view of this, the Deputy Director proposes that the chair approve and instruct this Committee and its subordinate institutions, all officers and soldiers, that when the national flag is raised or lowered in the future, they must face the direction of the national flag and stand at attention to salute. Those indoors should also stand at attention in this way, unless there are special obstructions. It is requested that this be forwarded to the superiors for clear instructions to all military and political institutions to follow uniformly, to emphasize etiquette and express reverence.' Therefore, after reviewing the above, the items presented are feasible. In addition to instructing this Committee and its subordinate institutions to comply, it is appropriate to prepare a document and request your Committee to instruct all military institutions and troops and schools to comply. Also, forward it to the National Government for instructions to the whole country to comply uniformly, to emphasize etiquette and express reverence.' Therefore, this should be implemented immediately. In addition to instructions and distribution, this order is issued for compliance and for forwarding to subordinate institutions for compliance. This order."

Grain Association Holds Meeting Yesterday, Resolves to Assist Overseas Chinese in Siam, Cables Central Government for Serious Negotiations, Unaware of Economic Severance 131

The Grain Trade Association of this city, for the sake of assisting overseas Chinese in Siam, held a full executive and supervisory committee meeting yesterday afternoon, resolving to notify fellow traders to adopt economic severance and cable the Executive Yuan, Chairman Chiang, the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, etc., for serious negotiations, and send a letter to the Siam overseas Chinese delegation expressing unanimous assistance. The Dagongshe reporter investigated and reported as follows:

Full Resolution: Economic Severance

Yesterday at 4:00 PM, the Grain, Oil, and Cake Trade Association held a full executive and supervisory committee meeting on the third floor of the Minguo Road Market. More than 20 people attended, including Gu Xinyi, Cai Yukun, Ye Tingfan, Wu Zisheng, Chen Ziyi, Zhu Zixiang, Feng Yongsheng, He Quansheng, He Xianggu, Yang Heqing, Yan Xiaoquan, Chen Yunqing, Chen Shaoming, Xia Xingcun, etc. The meeting was chaired by Gu Xinyi and recorded by Kong Rulin. First, the chairman reported on the petitioning delegation of overseas Chinese representatives in Siam and the letter from the Overseas Chinese Federation reporting the Siamese government's implementation of harsh policies and oppression. Then, each committee member stood up to express their opinions, and discussions began. The Siamese government's promulgation of harsh regulations to suppress overseas Chinese cannot be ignored by this association. In addition to cabling the central authorities, requesting them to make serious representations to the Siamese government, should effective sanctions be taken? (Resolution) If the Siamese government does not realize and improve the regulations, this association will notify fellow traders to sever economic ties with Siam.

Cable Central Government for Serious Negotiations

"To Premier Wang of the Nanjing Executive Yuan, Chairman Chiang of Guizhou, and Wang Junjian, Acting Minister of the Nanjing Ministry of Foreign Affairs: Having read the reports that the Siamese government has promulgated compulsory education and immigration laws, as well as various regulations for managing industry and commerce, on the one hand, implementing assimilation policies, and on the other hand, oppressing and restricting our country's immigrants and suppressing overseas Chinese industry and commerce, its insidiousness and cruelty have reached the extreme. If these regulations are implemented, our three million overseas Chinese will forever be reduced to Siamese slaves. This is of great concern to the future of the nation. We implore your (Chairman) (Seat) to quickly (instruct) (consult) the Ministry of Foreign Affairs (Your Ministry) to make serious representations to the Siamese government, to ensure the cancellation of the newly promulgated harsh regulations, protect our compatriots, and preserve our national dignity. The association will not forget its inadequacy and will resolutely adopt effective sanctions as a backing for the government. This urgent cable expresses our extreme apprehension. Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Shanghai Grain, Oil, and Cake Trade Association, kowtows, Geng."

Reply to Overseas Chinese Federation: Vow to be a Backing

"In reply, having received your letter, we have heard everything. The Siamese government's promulgation of various regulations, adhering to its psychology of bullying the weak, implements policies of suppressing overseas Chinese. If these are put into practice, three million overseas Chinese will be forever lost. Our country has historically been benevolent to the Siamese people, as history can attest. Now the Siamese government repays kindness with resentment. Its intentions are perverse, and its measures are misguided, which is extremely infuriating. All compatriots cannot ignore it. In addition to sending a cable to the Executive Yuan, Chairman Chiang, and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, requesting them to quickly make serious representations to the Siamese government and ensure the improvement of the newly promulgated regulations, this association will resolutely adopt effective sanctions as a backing for the government. We are writing in reply and hope you will take note. This is addressed to the Siamese Overseas Chinese Petition Delegation, the Overseas Chinese Federation Organizing Committee."

Since the beginning of spring, the climate of Shanghai has been unstable, with abnormal wind and rain. Although it was late spring last month, the cold wind was still biting. Municipal Party Headquarters Promotes Literacy Education: Notifies All Party Members to Launch a Unified Campaign 133

In order to actively promote literacy education, the Municipal Party Headquarters, in addition to formulating measures for party headquarters at all levels to promote literacy education and instructing all district party headquarters to prepare for establishment by June 20, also formulated measures for party members to teach the masses literacy and notified all party members to launch a unified campaign. Here is an excerpt from its letter to comrades: "Illiteracy is prevalent throughout our country. The number is staggering. Even in Shanghai, which is known as the economic hub and cultural center of the country, the number of illiterate people is probably higher than in the remote areas of Europe and the United States. The weakness of the nation and the decline of the people's spirit are not without reason. Because there are many illiterate people, culture will inevitably decline. Even if there are good methods to save the country and enthusiastic patriotic movements, it is still difficult to seek the understanding and support of the masses. If we look at the difficulty in implementing democracy and improving people's livelihood today, the reason is also known. Why are science and technology in Europe and the United States so prosperous, and why is construction so unhindered? Why are political facilities and social institutions so flexible in operation? This is because the level of public knowledge has been generally improved. Today, inventions and creations in various countries are heard from time to time, but even if our country catches up, it still cannot reach one ten-thousandth of their level. As a result, various theories are practiced in various countries and are all logical, but when applied to our country, they are not applicable everywhere. These are all obvious facts that can be known without further investigation. In view of this, our party has designated the literacy movement as one of the seven movements. At this time, the government is determined to eliminate illiteracy in the city, which is the time for us to work hard. Teaching one more person to read is to increase the strength of the country by one point, serve society, and benefit people. This is the right time. All comrades in the city must remember the importance of their mission and the need for civilian literacy, abide by the party's orders, work hard to promote it, and achieve complete success as soon as possible. We have high hopes for this."

League of Nations Water Conservancy Expert Nie Yufu Returned to Geneva Yesterday: Yellow River Development Can Hardly Be Delayed, Raising Huge Sums May Not Be Necessary 138

The Central News Agency reported that Nie Yufu, a water conservancy expert dispatched by the League of Nations to China for inspection, returned to Geneva yesterday morning on the Java Shipping Company's Zhishadani to report his mission. Guo Dehua, Secretary of the National Economic Council, represented the Council, and Heronmen, the Dutch Consul General in Shanghai, and others went to see him off. Mr. Nie's inspection in China this time has been very successful. According to the Central News Agency reporter's investigation with relevant parties, Mr. Nie has made a detailed investigation of the Yellow River water conservancy, believing that the dikes on both sides of the Yellow River are increasing day by day and the danger is increasing. They must be improved. He believes that the previous water conservancy experts' inspections of the Yellow River water conservancy, which required tens of millions of yuan to purchase machinery, contained the role of peddling machinery and were not for the sake of China itself. The development of Yellow River water conservancy and the prevention of floods do not necessarily rely entirely on machinery. Plows can also be used. Chinese farmers are extremely diligent and thrifty. Manpower can be used to dig a number of rivers between the two banks, which can prevent floods and irrigate the barren land and fields on both banks. This is one of the ways to develop the Yellow River water conservancy. If tens of millions of yuan are used to control the river, it may not be possible to raise the funds in a time of extreme social and economic panic, and the development of the Yellow River water conservancy cannot be delayed due to the difficulty of raising huge sums of money, he said.

Relief: Loans for Industry and Commerce 140

Anticipating Minister of Finance Kong's arrival in Shanghai, the implementation date will be determined.

According to the Central News Agency, the five million yuan relief loan for industry and commerce, after Minister Kong convened a meeting with leaders of the banking and financial industries to discuss the allocation of funds, the Bankers' Association has agreed to actively encourage subscriptions to raise 1.5 million yuan. Yesterday, a responsible person stated that one million yuan should be no problem, and that they will encourage subscriptions from banks with more ample funds for the remaining 500,000 yuan, with the possibility of reaching the full amount. On the financial industry side, although the managers of various member money houses resolved in a meeting the day before to maintain the original proposal of 250,000 yuan, the funds that each money house should subscribe have been submitted to the reserve of the Money Trade Association, and they can be handed over as soon as it is formally implemented. As for how to raise the remaining 750,000 yuan, it will be necessary to await the association's chairman, Qin Runqing, to report to Minister Kong and discuss it. The two and a half million yuan undertaken by the Central Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Bank of China have all been reserved. Various industrial and commercial sectors have expressed hope for early implementation to provide relief, as the amount already secured is 4.25 million yuan, which they suggest should be lent out first, and then find ways to raise the remaining amount. The banking community also shares this sentiment. However, whether to start immediately or wait until the full five million yuan is raised will depend on Minister Kong's arrival in Shanghai this morning and consultations with all parties.

Zhejiang Provincial Government to Borrow Spring Cocoon Loans from Shanghai Banks 141

1.8 Million Yuan at 8% Interest; Formal Signature After Drafting the Contract

According to the Central News Agency, the Zhejiang Provincial Government's Finance and Construction Departments negotiated with the banking community for a spring cocoon loan of 1.8 million yuan, which was decided at a meeting in Shanghai a few days ago, and a contract was drafted. After obtaining details, they are recorded as follows:

Drafting the Contract

Zhejiang Province is following the example of last year's autumn cocoon loan, borrowing 2 million yuan for spring cocoons from 14 banks including the Bank of China and the Bank of Communications in Shanghai. After first contacting the Hangzhou branches of each bank, Zeng Yangfu, Director of the Zhejiang Construction Department, came to Shanghai as a representative to convene the persons in charge of each bank. As a result of the meeting, it was decided to borrow 1.8 million yuan this spring because the 3 million yuan borrowed last autumn had not been exhausted. After each bank confirmed the amount they would borrow, a contract was drafted and taken to Hangzhou. The contract will be signed in the next few days after being approved by the Zhejiang Provincial Government. The interest rate is 8%, and there is no specified repayment period.

Loan Allocation

The allocation of the 1.8 million yuan loan among the banks is as follows: Bank of China, 450,000 yuan; Bank of Communications, 300,000 yuan; Zhejiang Industrial Bank, 240,000 yuan; Bank of Shanghai, 150,000 yuan; Ningbo Commercial Bank, 90,000 yuan; China Industrial Bank, 90,000 yuan; the Mainland Bank, Salt Industry Bank, Zhongnan Bank, Jincheng Bank, Zhejiang Industrial Bank, China National Goods Bank, China General Chamber of Commerce Bank, and China Reclamation Bank, each 60,000 yuan. The joint banking group will appoint the Bank of China, the Bank of Communications, and the Zhejiang Industrial Bank as representatives, as these three banks all have branches in Hangzhou, making it easier to collect and disburse funds and handle all related matters.

Repayment Method

The results of last autumn's loan were very good, but the 3 million yuan borrowed was not fully used. The provincial government needed funds to be disbursed by the banking group representatives at any time, and after the provincial government sold the cocoons and raw silk produced, the proceeds were returned to the banking group at any time. The amount currently borrowed has been gradually returned, and as of February, 190,000 yuan remained. It is expected to be fully repaid within a few months. The repayment method for this spring's orchid loan will also follow this method.

Zhejiang Provincial Fisheries Experiment Station Investigates Fish Fry Production Areas; Technicians Sent to Investigate the Upper Reaches of the Yangtze River 142

Dinghai correspondence: The Zhejiang Provincial Fisheries Experiment Station, recognizing the importance of fish fry, intends to send personnel to the upper reaches of the Yangtze River to investigate the spawning sites and spawning environment of grass carp, carp, and silver carp. However, due to the substantial costs involved, and because the fish fry of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, Hunan, and other provinces are all supplied by the Yangtze River, it is not a problem for Zhejiang Province alone. It is reported that the station has sent two technicians, Chen Chunshou and Lin Shuyan, with equipment to carry out the investigation. The estimated itinerary is two months, passing through the six provinces of Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hubei, and Hunan. Of all previous investigations of fish fry in China, this one is the largest in scale.

Proposed Establishment of a Commercial Union Bank; National Federation of Chambers of Commerce Offers Opinions 148

Units of Stores Still Have Untoward Matters; The Amount Per Share is Proposed to Be Increased to One Hundred Yuan

The Guangzhou Municipal Chamber of Commerce and others recently proposed to organize a National Commercial Union Bank and sent a letter to solicit the opinions of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce. A reporter from the Shin Shi News Agency specifically visited Lin Kanghou, chairman of the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, yesterday. According to Lin, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce recently received a letter from the Guangdong Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce proposing to organize a National Commercial Union Bank and providing a plan. The method is to unite chambers of commerce in various provinces and cities across the country to solicit shares from local stores, with each share priced at five yuan. Xiong Shaokang of the Guangdong Provincial Chamber of Commerce also made contact in person when he recently came to Shanghai. After research, a reply was given and several suggestions were made for their reference. It is believed that soliciting shares from local stores at five yuan per share is a good approach, but in practice, there are still difficulties. Therefore, it is considered that five yuan per share is too fragmented, and it should be at least one hundred yuan to suit general banking habits. At the same time, taking stores as the unit for shareholders, due to future inheritance rights and other relationships, is not appropriate, and it seems more appropriate to take people as the unit. The above-mentioned opinions have been sent to Guangdong for reference. Generally speaking, the National Commercial Union Bank may or may not be realized in the short term, but Guangdong may be expected to establish a Commercial Union Bank first and then seek expansion in the future.

Tax Affairs Administration Replies to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce; Imploring for the Cautious Indictment of Stamp Tax Cases 151

For Suspicious Cases, First Request Guidance From Superiors; The Municipal Chamber of Commerce is Requested to Re-Determine Procedures for Protesting

The Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce, due to the repeated occurrence of delivery receipts in this city that should not be stamped according to regulations but were inspected and fined, specially requested the Tax Affairs Administration to properly formulate preventive measures. A reply has been received from the Tax Affairs Administration adopting this, however, after the delivery receipt of the Heji Printing Company was fined and the protest was ineffective, the Chamber of Commerce sent a telegram to the Ministry of Finance, allowing it to protest again and return the fine. The original text is recorded below:

Tax Affairs Administration Reply Letter: Received your association's official letter Shangzi No. 412 and Shangzi No. 433, stating that the delivery receipts of Ruida, Datong, Heyuji, Maotai, and other coal shops were heavily fined, requesting that this type of delivery receipt should not be stamped according to regulations, ordering the inspectors in the concession to comply, and planning thorough preventive measures to avoid similar cases from happening again in the future, etc. With regard to the fact that the delivery receipt is the receipt for goods, there is no provision for stamping in the current Provisional Regulations on Stamp Tax, so it is not necessary to stamp. The current practice is to have the shop prepare a delivery receipt for the recipient to stamp. This delivery receipt is a receipt for goods, and according to the current Provisional Regulations on Stamp Tax, there is no requirement to affix stamps, so it is naturally not necessary to affix stamps. Regarding the matter of the Ruida and other coal shops' delivery receipts being fined, since it has been stated that an appeal has been filed, there will naturally be remedial measures. However, the fact that the inspectors arbitrarily prosecute, causing the shopkeepers to often suffer the loss of appeal expenses, is also true. When inspectors perform their duties, if they can follow the laws and regulations and carefully prosecute, or if they send suspicious cases to their superiors for review before imposing a fine, it will be sufficient to reduce future disputes. The Jiangsu Stamp Tax Bureau and the Shanghai Concession Inspection Office have been ordered to instruct their inspectors to comply. The above is the reply to your letter for your information.

Municipal Chamber of Commerce Telegram

Ministerial Office of the Ministry of Finance in Nanjing: According to the regulations and your ministry's interpretation, goods receipts within the special zone of this city do not require stamping, but they have been wrongly inspected and fined. According to the latest reports to this association, there have been four such cases. In two of these cases, fines of over one thousand yuan were imposed, and in the other two cases, fines of several hundred yuan were imposed. Small shops are afraid of losing their homes and going bankrupt. In three of these cases, the association has corresponded with the Tax Affairs Administration under your ministry to plan relief, but because the cases belong to the court, there are no appropriate measures. In the case of the Heji Printing Company, the result of the protest was still the original ruling. The only avenue of relief for merchants is almost zero. As the days get longer, what will happen? For the sake of urgent treatment, it is proposed that your ministry amend the regulations to allow for further appeals in such cases, and at the same time, send the past orders of your ministry regarding such cases to the Ministry of Judicial Administration for referral to courts at all levels for investigation and reference, in order to reduce the lack of communication. Before the measures for further appeals are stipulated, all fines of the Heji Printing Company and others that have been judged by the court but should not be borne in reality should be investigated and refunded in full to show fairness.

More Than Five Years After Being Killed by a Car; Cao's Father is Seventy Years Old and Destitute

The original text is recorded below: (1) Report to the Municipal Government: Regarding the case of Cao Yongkuan being injured and killed by an American Shanghai-based Naval Transport vehicle on November 29, 1929, his father has repeatedly petitioned your government, requesting a transfer to the American authorities for negotiations to compensate for injury and compensation. Since his son Yongkuan was injured and killed in an accident, he has been demanding compensation for more than five years, but nothing has been received. We earnestly request that your government transfer the matter to the American Consul General in Shanghai for prompt negotiation and payment of compensation. (2) Letter to the Public Works Department: Regarding the case of Cao Yongkuan being injured and killed by an American Shanghai-based Naval Transport vehicle on November 29, 1929, according to his father, Cao Zichang, who used to be a mechanic in the Electricity Department of the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, is now 71 years old, his life is difficult, and he is destitute. Since his son Yongkuan was injured and killed in an accident, he previously requested compensation from the authorities. More than five years have passed, and no compensation has been received. We request that you transfer the letter to your bureau and ask it to negotiate with the American authorities in Shanghai for prompt payment of compensation. We hereby request your bureau to investigate and handle the matter promptly. This is addressed to the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department. (3) Letter to the American Consul: Regarding the case of Cao Yongkuan being injured and killed by a Naval Transport vehicle of your country in Shanghai on November 29, 1929, the authorities have transferred the matter to your Consul General for compensation according to law. He is now 70 years old and destitute. He begs to transfer the letter to your Consul General for prompt payment of compensation in this case. After investigating the various allegations of Cao Zichang, the situation is indeed pitiable. We deeply hope that your Consul General will, based on the good friendship between our two governments and peoples, resolve this case satisfactorily. Not only will the relations between our two countries improve, but the reputation of your country's military will also increase. Based on the aforementioned situation, we hereby inform you and request that you investigate and handle the matter promptly. This is addressed to Mr. Clay Cosgrove, Consul General of the United States of America in Shanghai.

Liu Weishi Invents the Ring-Turning Three-Motion Electric Fan; The Ministry of Industry Has Approved a Five-Year Patent 155

Mr. Liu Weishi is from Gansu, Minxian County, and graduated from the Department of Political Economy of the Gansu College. He usually loves improving industrial equipment and has been buried in research for eighteen years. He has successively invented the inclined leather live shaft cotton gin, water-powered cotton gin, new type ink machine, simple seeder, new type gas lamp, etc., which have been greatly appreciated by the Gansu authorities. With the assistance of Shao Lizi, he recently successfully invented a ring-turning three-motion electric fan, which has been reviewed by the Ministry of Industry and approved for a five-year patent. Mr. Liu often comes to Shanghai and signed a contract with the local Huasheng Electric Appliance Factory to manufacture and sell the fan, which was also approved by the factory. The reporter met with him at his residence yesterday and asked about the fan's structure and function. He replied, "The small table fans we usually use only blow air in one direction or turn halfway, which is very inconvenient, so I (Liu) was determined to research and have now succeeded. There are six special parts for ring-turning and four parts for connecting electricity. In addition to being fixed and shaking its head, it can also turn a full circle, hence the name 'three-motion'. At the same time, I also felt that the range of the wind power was very small, and the wind emitted in the hot summer was still hot, so I made further research and successfully developed a spiral-blade fan, which is to change the ordinary fixed blades into spiral blades that can swing left, right, up and down, so that the range of its wind power can be expanded to 7.5 times larger than the current one. It is currently being submitted to the Ministry of Industry for review." As for the fact that the emitted wind is still hot, he is currently studying the principle of absorbing heat and emitting cold air, and is quite confident. However, he is suffering from the difficulty of raising test materials. When these electric fans are successfully produced and he has sufficient economic resources, he will continue to complete the vibratory cotton gin and spindle spinning machine that he invented three years ago. He had tested it more than seventy times, spending tens of thousands of yuan, and his family property was also exhausted as a result. Unfortunately, all the tools and plans were destroyed by bandits. If these things can be successful, I believe they will greatly benefit the textile industry in the future, because the current general spinning machines require the cotton to be ginned and then carded, which must go through several processes from coarse to fine before being fed to the spinning machine. What I am researching is to eliminate several times of drawing fine, which I have made considerable progress on. What I am most worried about and cannot bear to let fail is that I, who study political economy, should come and talk about invention. Every experiment is ridiculed by many, but I do not give up because of this. I must seek the truth in everything and then stop. Failure is certainly ashamed, but an occasional success makes relatives and friends change their attitude towards me, which is somewhat comforting. The success of a career is never accidental. In fact, failure can also be said to be success, because if you do not fail, you will not know how to fail like this. This is what I often use to console myself."
