Free Talk

Writing and Games 252

— 稜磨

Recently, someone joked that most Chinese people generally recognize characters like one, two, three, four, five, six, seven, eight, nine, ten thousand, center, fortune, east, west, south, north, etc., probably without needing to be taught. This is indeed humorous, but it seems to evoke more than just a lighthearted feeling. It contains a rather serious question, and the seriousness of the question isn't just the worrying spread of gambling, but rather whether literacy education can be promoted using games.

Gambling and games are only separated by a fine line. Mahjong is gambling, while Chinese chess and military chess are games. Military chess uses relatively complex characters, so it's mostly popular in schools. Chinese chess is popular in general society, and there are even those who can play chess without being literate, which gives them the opportunity to recognize characters like general, minister, scholar, elephant, advisor, pawn, chariot, horse, cannon, etc. Old-fashioned playing cards sometimes used phrases like "superior man," "Kong Yiji," etc., to form sets. Although these have become purely gambling tools today, perhaps the original purpose of making these toys was specifically to provide children with spelling practice. In Guangdong, there's a kind of large dice with the surnames Chen, Li, Huang, Qu, Ma, Mai, etc., engraved on its six sides. I don't know what it's used for, but it seems convenient for people to remember the most common surnames. Besides newly made toys that utilize characters, there must be quite a few older ones as well. If someone collected them to investigate whether they can help promote literacy education, I think it would be a worthwhile endeavor.

Chinese characters seem to have an inherent flaw that makes them unsuitable for use in toys. The lack of newly made character-based game toys is probably also due to this. When I was in middle school, a word-chain game in English was very popular among classmates, from "Have" to "Ever" to "Read." However, middle school students' English was limited, so the game wasn't very satisfying. Therefore, we switched to using Chinese characters. English is based on individual words, so we also used individual characters for Chinese. The method was from "娘" (niáng, mother) to "郎" (láng, gentleman) to "防" (fáng, defend). It seems that Liangyou Pictorial once held this game, and I don't know the results, but Liangyou sought the result of how many words a person could spell on their own, while the school game was a game of multiple people connecting. Chinese characters are more difficult to connect than English words. Therefore, our rule for this game was changed to whoever writes a word that others can't connect loses. This rule greatly reduced the number of characters needed, but it also made us discover that all Chinese characters with left-right or top-bottom structures that are used in many places are very effective characters. Now that I think about it, this game can be used to create Chinese spelling cards, similar to English spelling cards.

If we don't avoid colloquial characters, many simple-shaped characters can be very effective. For example, the characters 口 (kǒu, mouth), 木 (mù, wood), 土 (tǔ, earth), and 又 (yòu, again) can be combined to form thirty-two characters if we maximize their top-bottom and left-right relationships. Among them, at least twenty characters are recognizable words: 吐 (tù, vomit), 嘆 (tàn, sigh), 呆 (dāi, foolish), 呂 (lǚ, surname), 扣 (kòu, knock), 杜 (dù, surname), 权 (quán, authority), 林 (lín, forest), 杏 (xìng, apricot), 麥 (mài, wheat), 埜 (yě, wild), 堆 (duī, pile), 栽 (zāi, plant), 吉 (jí, lucky), 圭 (guī, jade tablet), 雙 (shuāng, pair), 桑 (sāng, mulberry), 聖 (shèng, saint), 綴 (zhuì, sew). In this way, if we carefully select fifty of the most effective radicals, we can probably spell more than a thousand common characters. This is not only convenient for learning, but also for typesetting if this method is adopted, it will definitely reduce the number of lead characters needed. In order to make Chinese characters easier to learn, it is necessary to increase the effectiveness of already familiar shapes and gradually eliminate rare shapes. The large number of strokes is not the biggest difficulty in learning characters. Although the character 龍 (lóng, dragon) has many strokes, it is worth the effort to learn because it is also used in more than twenty other common characters. The character 㐙 (kǎn), except for 侃 (kǎn, upright), has no other use, so even though it is not complex, it is a waste of energy to recognize it.

There are also many Chinese characters that are inherently very effective but are not often used as components of other characters, such as 二 (èr, two), 三 (sān, three), 六 (liù, six), 七 (qī, seven), 年 (nián, year), 上 (shàng, above), 西 (xī, west), etc. There are also characters that are very effective as components of other characters but are not very useful on their own, such as 丙 (bǐng, third), 酉 (yǒu, tenth), 兌 (duì, exchange), 氏 (shì, clan), 佳 (jiā, good), 睘 (qióng, to gaze), etc. These two should really be harmonized to achieve the best of both worlds. The characters that can be learned from previous applications and character games mostly only have value for independent use, so they are less effective. Now, if we know how to pay attention to their value in the structure of general characters, then character games are still worth promoting. In general, people are not lacking in interest in characters. Jokes about writing the character 萬 (wàn, ten thousand), character riddles about guessing the character 極 (jí, extreme), and anecdotes about 造字 (zào zì, creating characters) being 造錯 (zào cuò, creating mistakes), as well as character twisting and character breaking games, are all very popular, or even games created by people who are barely literate. These all show us that people pay the most attention to the analysis of characters, and we should really make use of this interest. I believe that at least for characters made up of two components, we can use spelling games to increase the opportunity for practice. Although this is a simple idea, if it can inspire people to create valuable plans that incorporate literacy education into games, it would be a "stroke of luck."

Idle Sorrow 253

— Wei Zhongtian

A pile of idle sorrow has been weighing on my heart like a stone for quite some time. In the past, when I was fighting the black hand of life all day long, idle sorrow was not allowed to exist in my heart. At that time, I only knew how to live, how to resist that black hand. But the current environment has changed a bit. This black hand of life is just hiding in a distant corner, not needing me to resist it. So, there is a lot of leisure time for me to reflect on the past and think about the future. In this situation, idle sorrow has taken root in my heart and is growing day by day.

I am not deliberately trying to be a moaner without illness; it is really that I feel I am too useless, and often see nothing but darkness before me. When I was young, my heart was full of hope, with my own small world of dreams. But as I get older, this hope gets smaller and smaller, and I think I am too insignificant. The kind of prayer that existed in my heart in my youth no longer exists.

A person's state of mind changes very easily. I have been very afraid of dusk lately. The color of dusk is like death. It seems that as soon as dusk descends, half of the world has died, and the stone in my heart also presses down especially hard. When a person reaches old age, it is like the day's journey has reached dusk. Dusk is a symbol of death for the elderly—regardless of how far away my age is from old age, seeing this symbol evokes feelings of disgust.

I have already seen the cherry blossoms, and my memories of them are not bad. I certainly sat under the cherry trees with friends, laughing and jumping, forgetting all the tears and sorrows of the world. However, this was only a fleeting moment. People love cherry blossoms, perhaps because they feel their lives are short and therefore love them? There are some things in the world that become more precious as their lives become shorter. This is a common feeling of mankind.

When old people see cherry blossoms, they recall everything from their youth—those dreams, those romances—and are probably filled with sighs, even if these sighs are not very strenuous. When young people see cherry blossoms, they think of the shortness of their own youth, and sing and dance to their hearts' content so as not to waste this youth...

Now it is the season when the cherry blossoms are withering again. When a gust of wind blows, you can see thousands and thousands of fallen petals floating in the air, floating on the ground, floating on your shoulders, and also floating in your heart. I cherish these petals like red maple leaves, clipping them in my diary. In the future, when I reopen this diary and see these petals, I wonder what my feelings will be?

Probably filled with sighs, right?

"The Petty Bureaucrat" 254

— Hu Kao

Miscellaneous Notes from Asahan (Continued) 255

— Fei Er

"That never happened again." Mr. Lin replied, "Firstly, because the Chinese were prepared; secondly, because the colonial government knew that the Chinese had great economic power in this area. Fearing that the society's economy would be affected, they dared not let the natives run wild again. But the most important reason is that the natives, influenced by the propaganda of the National Party members, recognized that their enemy was the white race, not the yellow race. Due to this shift in perspective, given time, the Chinese people's fears might turn into cooperation with the Malays, right?"

"Good, then let's celebrate their victory!" I couldn't help but clap my hands and laugh.

Mr. Lin was also drawn to laugh by my laughter.

By this time, night had fallen. A burst of brilliant electric lights illuminated the streets of Asahan; the dust of the day settled down in the cool tropical night. The streets gradually swelled with crowds, and a stuffy atmosphere stirred in the air. My eyes, exposed to the light of the electric lamps, made my head, confined to the hut on the banks of the Kualu River, feel slightly dizzy.

"Let's go to the suburbs to catch some wind!" I said.

So we walked together to the iron bridge over the Asahan River, which reached the Sudan Railway on the opposite bank.

Under the long iron bridge, the waters of the Asahan River appeared completely dark in the night. Only in one or two places, reflected by the lights, did a few patches of white appear, reflecting the wrinkles of the river. On the iron bridge, many overseas Chinese who were cooling off leaned against the bridge railings, gazing at the dark sky, or talking in low voices. The buildings of the railway station on the opposite bank were far away, enveloped in large shadows, but on the faces of the overseas residents illuminated by the lights, I could see many hearts, haggard and melancholy, hidden behind smiles.

The night breeze often brushed over our white clothes, making my mind clearer.

Many ships were moored on the riverbank. On the dark heaps, many faint lights shone out from the ships. On the opposite bank of the river, a large area of equatorial forest enveloped the earth in extraordinary darkness. (The End)

Rainy Journey 256

— Xu Ying

The rain was drizzling, and we parted ways.

This time, there were a total of eight people who came to Zhao Jiaji to issue loans: four guards from the security regiment, two bank accountants, Zhong Yu, and me. After the loans were issued, it started to rain lightly. According to the head of the Jia, we were supposed to stay in the market town for one night and leave in the morning, but the bank accountants wanted to return to the city to report, so we ordered the guards to escort the remaining funds and head to the city together.

Waving our hands, we parted ways. Zhong Yu and I rode our horses toward home.

The evening wind blew raindrops onto our faces, and our clothes slowly became damp. There hadn't been a sunny day for half a month, and the road was still muddy. We were traveling along a small path, which was a long embankment, with rivers and rice paddies on both sides. The sky was getting darker and darker every moment, and we didn't have lanterns, so we dared not gallop quickly.

There were few houses along the way, and we didn't encounter any pedestrians.

"Do you have weapons?" Zhong Yu asked from behind me, "I'm afraid..."

"What?" I turned around and asked, "Keep up..."

Listening carefully, there was indeed the sound of livestock footsteps behind us. Darkness covered the universe. Apart from the willow branches brushing our faces, the water waves turned dark and shiny, with a few boat lights. The rice paddies had lost their green color, and in the distance, it vaguely seemed like something was moving.

I comforted Zhong Yu, saying:

"Brother, how do you know it's not a traveling guest?"

"In the rain," Zhong Yu's voice trembled, "strangers wouldn't dare walk on the embankment."

While I was talking to embolden Zhong Yu, I was preparing. I held the hard weapons in my two riding breeches pockets. "Today, we are using the guise of issuing loans, and it is inevitable that we will be followed," I thought. I was a little anxious.

The distant hoofbeats were indeed following us. Slowly, we became aware that when we walked, he walked; when we stopped, he stopped. The two sides were always separated by a considerable distance. I was calculating that there were still two miles to the bottom of the embankment, and we could run when we reached the main road....

But, after walking another mile or so, I couldn't help but cry out in misery. The embankment was broken for about ten feet, and the villagers were drawing water. I desperately urged my horse to jump over it. The horse neighed loudly and shook its head, refusing to jump, so I desperately kicked its hind legs. I turned the horse's head and let Zhong Yu go over first. Zhong Yu's horse jumped over.

My horse still wouldn't jump.

The hoofbeats behind us grew closer and closer. And a strong light shot out from an electric baton, shining on us. The situation was critical. We were about to engage in close combat. I immediately took out the two boxes in my pockets and held them in my hands.

"Zhong Yu," I shouted, "fight them!"

My ready-to-fire posture was shrouded in the electric light for about a minute, and then the electric light disappeared. At this time, my horse naturally jumped over the ditch.

After passing the ditch, we listened quietly. The hoofbeats behind us did not follow, and no electric baton was shining on us either. I still dared not relax my grip on the two guns, remaining vigilant at all times.

Turning onto the main road, the rain stopped. Zhong Yu and I rode side by side.

"It seems he knows we have poor weapons and doesn't dare to chase us," Zhong Yu said. "He's still smart..." I smiled wryly in the darkness.

When we reached the village, I said to Zhong Yu:

"Lucky, lucky, there wasn't a single bullet in my two guns, if..."

We rejoiced that we hadn't encountered the "if." So, we could sleep peacefully again.

Rain (1) 257

— He Wei

The rain was falling mournfully. As soon as it dawned, Tian Li pushed open the window. Seeing the intermittent spring rain and the gloomy sky, he felt a knot form in his heart.

His uncle, lying on the couch, was still sound asleep, snoring loudly. Tian Li looked at his flat, round nose, the nose hairs that vibrated with each snore, the toothless mouth that revealed half a row of yellow teeth, and the honest, reserved face, and felt a little apologetic for disturbing his uncle's sleep on such a rainy day for his own selfish reasons.

"Let him sleep a little longer," he thought with a little pity. But when he thought about how long it had been since he last saw Juanzi, and how he didn't know when they would meet again after this trip to the north, his mood changed again. He felt restless all over, hot and bothered, even though the weather was so cold.

Indeed, he had always loved Juanzi. Juanzi had undoubtedly not changed her heart either, remaining as passionate and pure as ever, he knew. They were originally relatives, because she was his aunt's daughter. But her father was a high-ranking military officer, and her grandfather had also been influential in the late Qing Dynasty. Tian Li's father was just a farmer who guarded his fields, and their family was really too humble. This meant that they could not only not marry, but even meeting each other casually had to be arranged by their uncle, because the old grandmother who was inseparable from Juanzi and had raised her since her mother died was the most snobbish person, and almost got a headache whenever she saw Tian Li. This made him extremely painful. He wanted to ask Juanzi clearly if he could see her this time, whether she had the courage to leave her family.

As he thought, he ran to shake his uncle awake.

"Hmm, hmm, hmm..."

"Why are you always humming, Uncle, it's not early anymore!"

His uncle, who had been vaguely answering from under the covers, sat up quickly when he heard these words that were half joke and half reproach.

"It's not very good with the rain..."

Seeing the gloomy weather, his uncle stammered again, hesitating. He sat on the edge of the bed wrapped in a quilt, his mouth puckered as if he was in a very difficult situation.

"It doesn't matter, Uncle, you are always so suspicious. Can't Juanzi carry an umbrella on the road? Would her grandmother say that your house has a leaky roof and not allow her to go with you to stay at your house for a few days? No, be brave!"

Tian Li waited alone in a cool pavilion, while his uncle went to Juanzi's house alone. It was only a stone's throw away from her house, he could see it clearly, but he couldn't go. This made him gnash his teeth in hatred.

The pavilion was built in a narrow mountain gulch, not very high in altitude, but it could see far away. A stone mountain range wound around at his feet, disappearing into the barren fields at the foot of the mountain. Beyond the gray-purple grove of withered trees was the Zhijin River, where many small streams in the vicinity converged. Both sides were full of mountains, overlapping each other. Only the opposite side was a vast, barren plain—a gap.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Talking Points

"No Mission" and "Very Good Impression" 258

— Meng Ruo

If you are preparing to become an important person in the future, or if you are already among the ranks of important people, you should at least learn two "terms":—"No mission" and "Very good impression."

For example, suppose you have been entrusted with an important task by someone, the provincial government, or the central government, and you are going to a certain place to negotiate. As soon as you set off, word spreads, and nosy reporters will come to visit you everywhere, asking about the purpose of your trip. At this time, even if you are usually an honest person, you have no choice but to lie and answer him, "No mission." No mission, then what are you doing on this trip? You can vaguely tell him, "Going there to have fun," "Visiting some relatives and friends," or you can simply say, "Going to recuperate," if you have no concerns. If the purpose of your trip has some clues, no matter how you hide it, you can only answer, "I am not carrying any formal mission on this trip, but I am just going to talk as a private individual." Because important people do important things, if you tell the truth, "secrets of heaven cannot be revealed," things will be messed up, and it might even affect the overall situation. Therefore, the "term" "No mission" is the best magic weapon for important people to deal with reporters.

Next, let's talk about "Very good impression," which is also a very smooth "term" that can be used everywhere. People who are important people sometimes cannot avoid going to various places to inspect, or being sent abroad to investigate something. The results of the inspection or investigation are reported to others. Naturally, it is the reporters who ask for news. When you return from your inspection or investigation, and several reporters surround you and ask, "Sir, what are your thoughts on this inspection (or investigation) to a certain place (or country)?" This question is truly vast and boundless. It is easy to answer, and it can be answered well, but it is also difficult to answer. At this time, you may feel that there are too many thoughts, and you can't say them all at once. Or you may feel that there are too many things to say, and you don't know where to start. Or because you have only seen a superficial view, you can't find anything good to say. Or even though you have inspected or investigated for a few days, months, or even years, you have not inspected or investigated anything at all. However, this doesn't matter. Don't worry and think that this question is very difficult to deal with. Here I tell you, the four words "Very good impression" can be your guarantee, rescuing you from the reporters' encirclement. "Very good impression"—isn't this the most beautiful answer? As for whether the result of your inspection or investigation is indeed a very good impression, and in what aspects the impression is good, you can ignore this. Anyway, the reporters have received your answer, and they have news to write. No one will delve into the bottom of things.

A GlimPSE OF HONG KONG 259

— Hu Sizhong

The ship has passed the Seven Islands Sea. The moment we reach Chinese territorial waters, the homesickness of the travelers surges intensely:

"Oh, yellow motherland," your wanderer is about to fall into your embrace again!"

Seeing the deep blue of the Seven Islands Sea, I eagerly hope to reach Hong Kong quickly. Because once Hong Kong is reached, my gray hometown will be next.

Hong Kong has indeed arrived. First, a cluster of beautiful small islands, one after another, lined up in the sea. Green grass covers the land, making the mountain scenery as delicate as a young girl's face. Each hill is short and small. The ship passes by, making them look like children's toys. The seawater gradually fades from deep blue, eventually turning into light green. The ship travels in the vast ocean, seemingly without end. Once it enters the mountains of Hong Kong, it slows down, as if to allow the guests to enjoy the South China Sea's

Page 20

mountain scenery, to ease the boredom of the four or five days of the hazy sea voyage.

Hong Kong appears to the traveler with its Westernized buildings. Although the territory has not yet gone beyond the British Empire's colony, seeing the Guangdong sampans filling the sea and hearing the noisy sounds of the Chinese citizens on the shore, one feels a sense of relief, because from now on, we are regaining the status of ordinary Chinese people, no longer like the people living in the colony.

The ship stopped in the waters of Hong Kong, and the friends traveling together suggested going to the mountain for fun. After four long days of drifting on the vast sea, how lovely the land feels to the sea travelers!

After inquiring about the departure time of the ship, everyone jumped onto a small electric boat that takes passengers up the mountain. When walking down the steep stairs, people repeatedly warned:

"The pickpocketing skills in Hong Kong are very high. Look, pay attention to those opium addicts with coats or raincoats rolled up on their arms! Watch out for your wallet. They think you are rich overseas Chinese returning home!"

I smiled and stepped into the small electric boat. With a whistle, the small electric boat started. The sea is full of ships of all sizes, and the boat women are rowing wooden oars, their sounds constantly spreading around.

Looking at the buildings layered on top of each other in front of me, it's very pleasing to the eye. It's a pity that it's not night, so I can't immediately see the beautiful and famous night view of Hong Kong. And with limited time, Hong Kong cannot be fully enjoyed.

The pier is very noisy. Everyone quickly grabbed a dim sum, walked through several large companies, and hired a car for a trip up the mountain. The streets in Hong Kong are very narrow and there are many pedestrians, so the car doesn't move smoothly. Once it leaves the suburbs and climbs on the deserted mountain roads, it becomes very fast. The various views of the sea, like scenes in a movie, are shown one after another. The houses, trees, bridges, and famous trams going up and down the mountain are also gradually reflected in the eyes. The city noise is very low from above, allowing us to fully appreciate the beautiful scenery. However, due to time constraints, we cannot make a more complete and thorough inspection of this important eastern colony, so we can only make a reservation first, and wait for a few days of free time to come and inspect this small island again.

Hastily, the sails on the sea and the small and exquisite villa-style buildings on the mountain flashed past the corner of my eye. Chinese citizens passed by the car in various postures, and the groups of rulers of the colony were sparsely left behind. We followed the ship's scheduled departure time and stepped out of Hong Kong's borders again.

In the afternoon, the ship sailed eastward, and Hong Kong gradually shrank behind us until it disappeared. Therefore, I felt that these few hasty glimpses were not impressive enough, and I regretted not being able to see Hong Kong at night. Since then, I thought it would be easy to see the small island of Hong Kong again, but it has not yet been realized, which is truly filled with longing and yearning.

"When will I be able to see Hong Kong again?" I often ask myself this.

SILKWORM WOMAN 260

— Wu Fei

On Qingming Day, the weather was mild and sunny. In the azure blue sky, except for a few wisps of milky white clouds drifting slowly, only a round sun was smiling down on the earth, its mouth wide open. The warm breeze brought intoxicating floral fragrances, blowing on Jinrong's sister-in-law, making her feel a little dazed. The mulberry trees in front of the door had already grown leaf lobes the size of foreign coins. Jinrong's sister-in-law was about to move all the silkworm rearing tools piled on the shelves down, carry them to the river to wash them clean, and then paste a layer of white paper on the bottom of the rearing trays, and carefully paste a red paper-cut of the Silkworm Flower Prince or Silkworm Flower Goddess, in preparation for receiving silkworm ants. Because Jinrong's sister-in-law was alone, she only raised two sheets of silkworm eggs. But even with just two sheets, if the silkworms grew well, it would be tiring enough for her alone.

In the days close to Grain Rain, she would always open the silkworm eggs tucked in her chest twice a day to see if they were developing evenly. When she saw dense, furry things wriggling on the seed paper, she skillfully and with experience took out the seed paper, put it in a small rearing tray, and placed it on a slightly warm wok on the stove to melt them. At the same time, she took a few dried winter mulberry leaves that she had picked last year, dried them over the fire, and ground them into powder. She also broke off a few cherry pits and some pomegranate buds to sprinkle on the seed surface. Later, she cut a few wild peach branches at the back door, and all the doors, including the main door, back door, and room door, were filled with them. She also put a branch in the small rearing tray for melting silkworm ants.

Finally, she ran to the mulberry field and picked a handful of tender leaves. After chopping them extremely fine on the leaf-chopping stool, she cautiously carried the small rearing tray and placed it on the table in front of the ancestral hall. Using a scale rod, she lifted the seed paper and gently wiped all the silkworm ants onto the small rearing tray with a large goose feather, then spread a layer of finely chopped mulberry leaves on the ant surface.

The silkworm rearing tray was placed inside the bed. She had to get up at least three times every night to spread leaves. The mulberry leaves were eaten down day by day, and the silkworm bodies grew larger day by day. From black, they turned gray, and then completely transformed from gray to white skin. At the same time, Jinrong's sister-in-law's work also became more intense.

For the first sleep, one small rearing tray became three medium rearing trays. For the second sleep, three medium rearing trays had turned into five large rearing trays. When it came to emerging from the fire - the third sleep - she was even busier. On the one hand, she was picking and cutting mulberry leaves, and on the other hand, she had to catch sleeping silkworms and get rid of silkworm droppings. Especially when she saw that it was about to rain, she had to rush to grab leaves at all costs. If it suddenly rained heavily one day, even under a torrential downpour, she had to cut leaves.

For the sake of the silkworms, she often didn't even have time to eat meals or have a fixed number of meals. She didn't even have fixed sleep, especially after catching the big sleep, she barely got four hours of good sleep a night. However, looking at those lively silkworms with mottled and white skin, they were indeed lovely. Listening to them eating leaves, the rustling sound was like heavy rain, and a unique, pungent fragrance filled the silkworm house.

First molting, second molting... Although she had encountered several heavy rains in between, she was fortunate to have prepared enough overnight leaves in advance, so no major panic occurred. However, during the night of the big sleep, a heavy thunderstorm kept her company at the silkworm table all night without closing her eyes.

A month passed quickly, the silkworms were old, and Jinrong's sister-in-law was thin.

Now, in the living room and wing rooms, everything had turned into clusters of snow-white, adorable cocoon mountains. She was extremely happy. Although it was the result of more than a month of hard work and effort, having so many snow-white cocoons could at least comfort her.

"SIR, I DARE NOT!" 261

— Written by Zhu Yanghui

BEIJING PEOPLE'S "TEA DRINKING" 262

— Yueshan

"Tea drinking" is very common in our country. Regardless of north or south, regardless of elegance or vulgarity, everyone likes tea. Beijing people's "tea drinking" is very famous. Apart from the refined scholars and elegant gentlemen, even peddlers and commoners often make "tea drinking" a habit. What I want to talk about is this type of people's tea drinking. I haven't tasted the taste of the elegant people's tea tasting, so I won't talk about it.

In Beijing, tea houses are as numerous as sesame cake shops and sliced noodle shops. No matter on the main streets or small alleys, sesame cake shops can be seen everywhere. In Beijing mornings, the calls of sesame cake vendors can be heard at any time on every alley. The number of sesame cake shops is visible, and the number of tea houses is the same. One of the reasons is that sesame cake shops often turn into tea houses in the afternoon.

There are also tea houses that do not belong to sesame cake shops, because sesame cake shops are busy making sesame cakes in the morning and do not have the time to sell tea. For those who want to drink morning tea, many tea houses have become professional, not making sesame cakes.

Anyone who has been to Beijing has probably seen such signs: a rope tied to a piece of mahogany board, with cloth strips tied under the board. The board is written with words such as "Before the Rain," "Tip of the Tongue," "Fragrant Flakes," etc. That is the tea house. Some tea houses also hang many paper balls, with paper strips hanging from the paper balls, like an umbrella: That is the sesame cake shop (or sliced noodle shop, those paper strips represent the meaning of noodles.) that also serves as a tea house.

This is the appearance of Beijing tea houses, which is slightly different from those in Nanjing, Suzhou, Guangzhou, etc.

The patrons of this type of tea house, apart from a small portion of idle people carrying birdcages, are mostly laborers. They are not going to "taste tea." They are there to recover from fatigue, to make their bodies and minds feel refreshed. At a very low price, they gather a few close friends, talk, laugh,

Page 21

Page 22

laugh, and sometimes maybe scold a little. It is their entertainment.

Sometimes this phenomenon can be seen: two rickshaw pullers, both sweating, are pulling their respective customers. When they face each other, one says: "Hey, see you at Eryouxuan tonight." The other echoes: "Definitely, I'll wait for you." Then each goes his own way. That is pulling a close friend to drink tea. Tea houses are not lonely places. Strangers quickly become friends. Even if they have never met before, face to face, teapot to teapot, I pour you a cup, you pour me a cup, and then they start talking, talking about life, talking about social news. Sometimes they also scold, this donation and that donation are all on the list of things being scolded... Their conversations. seems to have no distance at all. How is the weather, what is your honorable surname, these are rarely mentioned. They are all sincere, all bold, and they can talk about anything. After they finish, they each go their own way, like close acquaintances, but in reality, they haven't even exchanged names. The nature of Northerners can be seen from here.

This way of drinking tea is not expensive. The tea leaves can be brought by oneself, and a large piece of "Gaomo" (i.e., leaf ends) can be drunk for half a day, while the water fee is only three or four cents per person, which can be said to be extremely proletarian. As for storytelling places and summer tea sheds, they are relatively expensive. This type of tea drinking probably costs no less than about ten cents. The most expensive is of course the tea seats in the park, which usually cost ten cents per person. If you invite two or three friends and crack one or two plates of melon seeds, it is already about one yuan. This should belong to the "tea tasting" category, which will not be discussed here.

MOVIE NEWS

FILM CITY 266

"The Beginning of Man" filmed a street scene yesterday. Although there were only seven or eight shots, there were more than 500 actors. Shi Dongyou and Zhou Kezhen were sweating profusely.

Next door to Yihua Company is Jiangnan College. Recently, Jiangnan College moved, and the Chinese Women's Sports Teachers College moved in. Yesterday morning, Hu Ping went to the company because she had a scene in "The Beginning of Man." When she passed the school, she was seen by more than 20 girls standing at the school gate. After a burst of "Look at Hu Ping" shouts, they all surrounded Hu Ping in the center. At this time, the embarrassing expression on Hu Ping's face was truly profound.

Yue Feng's new script has been completed and will soon be sent to Beijing for inspection. The female lead has been chosen to be Ye Juanjuan, who received good reviews in "The Flight." Ye Juanjuan has been particularly diligent in practicing "Mandarin" these days.

Newcomer Zhang Fei plays the role of a boat girl in "The Beginning of Man." Although it is her first time on camera, she performs quite naturally.

Miss Ge Aina, a graduate of Tsinghua School in Beijing, has officially joined Yihua. She has a role in "The Storm," which is another clear demonstration of Yihua's promotion of newcomers.

Yuan Meiyun plays Wei Heling's daughter-in-law in "The Beginning of Man," but she plays Wei Heling's daughter in "The Storm."

Fang Peilin, the set designer for "The Beginning of Man" and "The Storm," has recovered from his toothache, and his specialty, "Ventriloquism," is also performed as usual.

Chen Linshu, the stage manager of Yihua, is getting fatter day by day, and is on the verge of catching up with Yin Cenxiu.

Yan Chuntang, the general manager of Yihua, is proficient in Tai Chi. Anyone who asks for instruction is granted without exception.

"NATIONAL CUSTOMS" GRAND OPENING 267

Since Ms. Ruan Lingyu's last work, "National Customs," opened at the Jincheng Grand Theater, it has been a week in the blink of an eye. In terms of box office, it has always been crowded. Ruan Lingyu's past works have never disappointed people. This last work is even more noteworthy, not to mention that the cast of this film, in addition to Ruan Lingyu, also includes Lin Chuchu, Li Lili, Zheng Junli, Luo Peng, Liu Jiqun and other big stars. The red flowers and green leaves complement each other, and the directing skills of Luo Mingyou and Zhu Shilin are also very lively and agile. A very serious subject is written with extremely fancy techniques, giving people a feeling of both crying and laughing everywhere.
